Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Joint Purchase Options: When One Buyer Consents
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of one buyer's consent on the other's option in joint purchases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions (Imam vs. Sahibayn) on whether a co-buyer's option survives after one buyer consents, and explain the illa (cause) for each position.

Core Idea
A co-buyer's consent cancels the other's option according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but not according to the two disciples.

This passage delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute over the effect of one buyer's exercise of an option when two purchase jointly. The matn rules that the option is cancelled by one's consent, but the commentary reveals a deeper conflict between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples. Understanding their arguments—centered on the concept of 'ayb al-shirkah (defect of partnership)—is crucial for grasping Hanafi contract law and the balancing of rights between buyers and sellers.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the matn's ruling
Two persons buy an item jointly with a stipulated option (khiyar al-shart). The matn says the option is cancelled by the consent of one of them. Identify that this is the base ruling from the text.
The matn also applies this to khiyar al-'ayb and khiyar al-ru'ya.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The commentary reveals that Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the option is indeed cancelled, while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that each buyer's option is independent.
3
Analyze Imam Abu Hanifa's dalil
Imam argues that if the other buyer returns the item after one has consented, the seller would receive an item that is now partially owned by the consenting buyer – a defect of partnership ('ayb al-shirkah). This harms the seller.
The commentary elaborates: the seller could previously use the item freely; after return, he must share it.
4
Analyze Sahibayn's dalil
Sahibayn argue that the option is legislated to prevent deception (ghabn). Each buyer has an independent need for protection, so one's action cannot nullify the other's right.
This is also the view of the three other imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical difference: under Imam, the other buyer cannot rescind; under Sahibayn, he can. The text does not declare a mufta bihi, but later Hanafi practice often prefers Imam's view to protect the seller.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخيار شرط المُشتَريَيْن يَسْقُط برضا أحدِهِما، وكذا خيار العيب والرُّؤْيَةِ وخيار شرط المُسْتَرِيَيْنِ يَسْقَط برضا أحدهما، وكذا خيار العيب والرُّؤْيَةِ) : لأَنَّه إن ردَّه الآخر يكون معيباً بعيب الشركة، وعندهما للآخرِ ولاية الرَّد ؛ لأنَّ الخيار ثابت لكل واحد [1] قوله : وخيار.... الخ ؛ حاصله : أنه إذا اشترى رجلان شيئا على أنهما بالخيار، فرضي أحدهما بالبيع بأن أسقط خياره، ليس للآخر قدرة الرد عند الإمام خلافاً لهما ، فأنهما قالا : له أن يردّه ، وهو قول الأئمة الثلاثة. أحدهما وعلى هذا خيار العيب ؛ بأنه إذا اشترى رجلان شيئاً على خيار العيب فرضي بعيب فيه للآخر، وكذا خيار الرؤية، بأنه لو اشتريا شيئاً لم يرياه ثم رأى أحدهما ورضي لا الآخر. [٢] قوله : برضـا أحدهما ؛ قال شيخنا العلامة الطحطاوي في «حاشيته على الدُّرِّ المختار»: «ذكر الرضاء اتفاقي؛ إذ لو ردّ أحدهما لا يجيزه الآخر، ولم أره صريحاً، لكن قولهم : لو ردّه لردّ معيبا يدل عليه». انتهى (۳) قوله : لأنه إن رده الخ؛ حاصله : أن المبيع لما خرج عن ملك البائع لم يكن معيباً بعيب الشركة ، فلو ردّه أحدهما لا الآخر ردّه معيباً بعيب الشركة ؛ لأنَّ الشركة في الأعيان المجتمعة عيب؛ لأن البائع بتقدير الردّ لا يتمكن بالانتفاع به إلا بطريق التهايؤ، وكان قبل البيع متمكنا من الانتفاع متى شاء، وهذا إلزام ضرر زائد. فإن قيل : البائع قد رضي بردّ أحدهما ؛ لأنه خيرهما، فإلزام الضرر برضاه لا بغيره، ولا مضائقة فيه. قلنا : ليس من لوازم إثبات الخيارِ لهما الرّضاء برد أحدهما ، فإن البائع لعله تصوّر اجتماعهما على الردّ فتحقق الانفكاك ، فكيف يلزم الرضاء بردّ أحدهما إثبات الخيار لهما. كذا في حواشي «الهداية». [٤] قوله : لأن الخيار ... الخ ؛ حاصله : أنّ الخيار ثابت لكل واحد منهما ؛ لأنه شرع دفعاً للغبن، وكلّ واحدٍ منهما محتاج إلى دفعه عن نفسه، فكيف يسقط الخيار بإسقاط صاحبه ؛ لأن فيه إبطال حقه.
And the option of condition of two buyers is cancelled by the consent of one of them, and similarly the option of defect and the option of inspection, and the option of condition of two sellers is cancelled by the consent of one of them, and similarly the option of defect and the option of inspection) because if the other returns it, it would be defective with the defect of partnership. And according to the two (disciples), the other has the authority to return because the option is established for each one. [1] His statement: 'and the option... etc.' – its summary: if two men buy something with the condition that they both have the option, and one of them consents to the sale by cancelling his option, the other does not have the power to rescind according to Imam, contrary to the two disciples, for they said: he may return it, and it is the statement of the three Imams. And upon this is the option of defect: if two men buy something with the option of defect and one is satisfied with a defect in it for the other, and similarly the option of inspection: if they buy something they have not seen, then one sees it and is satisfied, the other does not (have the right to rescind). [٢] His statement: 'by the consent of one of them' – our master al-Tahtawi said in his Hashiya on al-Durr al-Mukhtar: 'The mentioning of consent is incidental, because if one returns, the other does not authorize it, and I did not see it explicitly, but their statement: if he returns it, he returns it defective, indicates it.' (۳) His statement: 'because if he returns it... etc.' – its summary: when the sold item left the ownership of the seller, it was not defective with the defect of partnership. So if one of them returns it without the other, he returns it defective with the defect of partnership, because partnership in combined property is a defect, because the seller upon return cannot benefit from it except through division (tahayu'), whereas before the sale he could benefit whenever he wished. This imposes excessive harm. If it is said: the seller consented to the return of one of them because he gave them the option, so imposing harm is with his consent and not others, and there is no difficulty in it. We say: it is not necessary that establishing the option for them implies consent to the return of one of them, for perhaps the seller envisioned their mutual agreement on return, so the separation materialized; how can consent to return of one be necessary from establishing the option for them? Thus in the marginalia of al-Hidayah. [٤] His statement: 'because the option... etc.' – its summary: the option is established for each one of them because it is legislated to prevent deception, and each one needs to repel it from himself, so how can the option be cancelled by the cancellation of his companion, because that would nullify his right?
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario where two persons jointly purchase an item with a stipulated option (khiyar al-shart), or with options of defect (khiyar al-'ayb) or inspection (khiyar al-ru'ya). The matn states that the option is cancelled by the consent of one of them. The commentary explains that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, if one buyer cancels his option (by expressing satisfaction), the other buyer loses the right to rescind the sale. This is because returning the item after one buyer has consented would cause a defect (partnership) in the item, harming the seller. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, holding that each buyer's option is independent; the other buyer can still rescind. This is also the view of the three other imams (Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad). The passage then analogizes to khiyar al-'ayb: if two buyers buy something with an option due to defect, and one is satisfied with the defect, the other can still return it? Actually, the text says 'and upon this is the option of defect' meaning the same dispute applies: Imam says no, Sahibayn say yes. Similarly for khiyar al-ru'ya. The commentary further clarifies that the word 'consent' is used incidentally; if one actually returns the item, the other cannot authorize it. Then there is a discussion of why returning by one creates a defect: the item was in perfect condition when sold; after purchase, it becomes co-owned, and returning only a share makes it defective because the seller cannot use it freely without division. This harm is not offset by the seller's initial agreement to grant options, because he likely assumed both would agree on a decision. Thus, Imam's position prevents harm to the seller and maintains the integrity of the sale. The disciples' position emphasizes that each buyer's right to protect himself from deception (ghabn) is independent, and one's choice should not nullify the other's right. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated here, but later Hanafi works often prefer Imam's view in this matter.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated in a contract allowing one or both parties to cancel or confirm the sale within a specified period
خيار العيب (khiyar al-'ayb): The option to rescind a sale due to a defect in the sold item that was unknown at the time of contract
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'ya): The option to rescind a sale after viewing an item that was purchased unseen
عيب الشركة ('ayb al-shirkah): A defect arising from co-ownership; the fact that an item becomes owned by multiple parties is considered a legal defect that harms the seller's ability to use the item freely

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa for cancelling the other buyer's option when one buyer consents?
A) Because the option is a single right that cannot be divided.
B) Because returning the item would create a defect of partnership harming the seller.
C) Because the seller only intended to sell to both together.
D) Because the disappearing buyer must also consent.

Key Takeaway
The consent of one joint buyer cancels the other's option according to Imam Abu Hanifa to prevent harm to the seller, but the two disciples uphold each buyer's independent right.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Joint Buyers' Option: When One Waives
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar al-shart

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar al-shart for joint buyers and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
One buyer's waiver does not nullify the other's option to reject.

This passage explores a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: when two buyers jointly purchase with a stipulated option and one waives his right, does the other still have the right to reject? Imam Abu Hanifa says no, citing harm to the seller from the defect of partnership. The Sahibayn say yes, as each option is established independently to prevent deception. Later Hanafi authorities adopt the Sahibayn's view, which also aligns with the other three Imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling in dispute
The act is the purchase of an item by two buyers with a stipulated option (khiyar al-shart). The ruling in dispute is whether the other buyer can still reject the sale after one buyer has waived his option.
The dispute applies also to khiyar al-'ayb and khiyar al-ru'yah.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and its dalil
Abu Hanifa holds that the other buyer loses the right to reject. His proof: if the other buyer returns the item, it would be returned with a defect of partnership (since one buyer's share remains), causing harm to the seller.
The defect of partnership means the seller would get back a co-owned item, not full ownership.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their dalil
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the other buyer retains the right to reject. Their proof: the option is established for each buyer individually to prevent deception; one person's waiver cannot nullify another's right.
This is also the view of the three other Imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to the objection
The text addresses a possible objection: the seller consented to the possibility of a single return by granting the option. The rebuttal: giving the option to both jointly does not imply consent to a return by only one; the seller likely envisioned them acting together.
This response shows the depth of the legal reasoning.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Later authorities like al-Tahawi and the glosses of al-Hidayah prefer the Sahibayn's view. It is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
The mufta bihi aligns with the majority of the school and other madhahib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخيار شرط المُشتَريَيْن يَسْقُط برضا أحدِهِما، وكذا خيار العيب والرُّؤْيَةِ وخيار شرط المُسْتَرِيَيْنِ يَسْقَط برضا أحدهما، وكذا خيار العيب والرُّؤْيَةِ) : لأَنَّه إن ردَّه الآخر يكون معيباً بعيب الشركة، وعندهما للآخرِ ولاية الرَّد ؛ لأنَّ الخيار ثابت لكل واحد. [١] قوله : وخيار.... الخ ؛ حاصله : أنه إذا اشترى رجلان شيئا على أنهما بالخيار، فرضي أحدهما بالبيع بأن أسقط خياره، ليس للآخر قدرة الرد عند الإمام خلافاً لهما ، فأنهما قالا : له أن يردّه ، وهو قول الأئمة الثلاثة. أحدهما وعلى هذا خيار العيب ؛ بأنه إذا اشترى رجلان شيئاً على خيار العيب فرضي بعيب فيه للآخر، وكذا خيار الرؤية، بأنه لو اشتريا شيئاً لم يرياه ثم رأى أحدهما ورضي لا الآخر. [٢] قوله : برضـا أحدهما ؛ قال شيخنا العلامة الطحطاوي في «حاشيته على الدُّرِّ المختار»: «ذكر الرضاء اتفاقي؛ إذ لو ردّ أحدهما لا يجيزه الآخر، ولم أره صريحاً، لكن قولهم : لو ردّه لردّ معيبا يدل عليه». انتهى (۳) قوله : لأنه إن رده الخ؛ حاصله : أن المبيع لما خرج عن ملك البائع لم يكن معيباً بعيب الشركة ، فلو ردّه أحدهما لا الآخر ردّه معيباً بعيب الشركة ؛ لأنَّ الشركة في الأعيان المجتمعة عيب؛ لأن البائع بتقدير الردّ لا يتمكن بالانتفاع به إلا بطريق التهايؤ، وكان قبل البيع متمكنا من الانتفاع متى شاء، وهذا إلزام ضرر زائد. فإن قيل : البائع قد رضي بردّ أحدهما ؛ لأنه خيرهما، فإلزام الضرر برضاه لا بغيره، ولا مضائقة فيه. قلنا : ليس من لوازم إثبات الخيارِ لهما الرّضاء برد أحدهما ، فإن البائع لعله تصوّر اجتماعهما على الردّ فتحقق الانفكاك ، فكيف يلزم الرضاء بردّ أحدهما إثبات الخيار لهما. كذا في حواشي «الهداية»(۳). [٤] قوله : لأن الخيار ... الخ ؛ حاصله : أنّ الخيار ثابت لكل واحد منهما ؛ لأنه شرع دفعاً للغبن، وكلّ واحدٍ منهما محتاج إلى دفعه عن نفسه، فكيف يسقط الخيار بإسقاط صاحبه ؛ لأن فيه إبطال حقه.
And the option of stipulation for two buyers falls by the consent of one of them, and likewise the option of defect and sight and the option of stipulation for two sellers falls by the consent of one of them, and likewise the option of defect and sight: because if the other returns it, it would be defective with the defect of partnership. And according to them (the two disciples), the other has authority to reject because the option is established for each one. [1] His saying: 'And the option...' etc.; its summary: When two men buy something with the condition that they have the option, and one of them is pleased with the sale by dropping his option, the other does not have the power to reject according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa), contrary to them (the two disciples), for they said: He may reject it, and it is the saying of the three Imams. One of them: And upon this is the option of defect; for when two men buy something with the option of defect and one is pleased with a defect in it, the other [may reject], and likewise the option of sight, for if they bought something they had not seen, then one saw and was pleased but not the other. [2] His saying: 'by the consent of one of them'; our teacher, the Allamah al-Tahawi said in his Gloss on al-Durr al-Mukhtar: 'Mentioning consent is incidental; for if one rejects, the other does not authorize him, and I did not see it explicitly, but their saying "if he returns it he would return it defective" indicates it.' End. (3) His saying: 'because if he returns it' etc.; its summary: That since the sold item left the ownership of the seller, it was not defective with the defect of partnership, so if one of them returns it without the other, he would return it defective with the defect of partnership because partnership in combined physical assets is a defect, because the seller, upon the hypothetical return, cannot benefit from it except through division of use, whereas before the sale he was able to benefit whenever he wished, and this is imposing an additional harm. If it is said: The seller has consented to the return by one of them because he gave them the option, so imposing harm is with his consent, not otherwise, and there is no hardship. We say: It is not necessary from establishing the option for them that he consents to the return by one of them, for perhaps the seller envisioned them both together on rejection so the separation occurs, so how can consent to return by one of them be necessitated by establishing the option for them? Thus in the glosses of al-Hidayah. (3) [4] His saying: 'because the option' etc.; its summary: That the option is established for each one of them because it is legislated to prevent deception, and each one of them needs to prevent it from himself, so how can the option be dropped by the dropping of his companion? Because that would nullify his right.

Commentary
Intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states that when two buyers purchase jointly with a stipulated option (khiyar al-shart), the option falls if one of them consents (i.e., waives his option). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the other buyer then loses his right to reject the sale. However, according to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), the other buyer still has the right to reject. The same applies to khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect) and khiyar al-ru'yah (option of sight). The reason for Abu Hanifa's position is that if the other buyer returns the item, it would be returned with a defect of partnership (since the item is now co-owned between the returning buyer and the seller's original partner? Actually careful: The text says 'because if he returns it, it would be defective with the defect of partnership.' The commentary explains that once the sale is concluded, the item is out of the seller's ownership. If one buyer returns his share, the item would come back to the seller but partially owned by the other buyer? Actually more precisely: When two buyers purchase jointly, they become co-owners. If one waives his option and the sale is binding on him, his share remains with him. If the other then tries to return the entire item, that would return it with a co-ownership share that is not being returned, thus making it defective from the seller's perspective. The seller would get a part-ownership rather than full ownership, which is considered a defect. Abu Hanifa says because of this harm to the seller, the option of the other is also dropped when one waives. The disciples argue that the option is established for each individually to protect each from deception, so one's waiver should not affect the other's right. The commentary also addresses a possible objection: that the seller consented to the possibility of one return by giving the option. The rebuttal is that giving the option to both jointly does not imply consent to a single return; the seller likely expected both to agree on return. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) according to later Hanafi authorities, as it is the view of the three Imams (Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad?) actually the text says 'it is the saying of the three Imams', meaning the other three madhhabs.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): The option to confirm or rescind a sale that is stipulated at the time of contract, valid for up to three days in the Hanafi school.
عيب الشركة ('ayb al-shirkah): A defect arising from partnership of ownership, meaning that the item is jointly owned, which prevents the owner from full unrestricted use.
الرد (al-radd): The act of rejecting the sale and returning the item to the seller within the option period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, if two buyers jointly purchase an item with a stipulated option and one waives his option, what is the status of the other buyer's right to reject?
A) The other buyer's option also falls.
B) The other buyer still has the right to reject the sale.
C) The sale becomes void automatically.
D) The seller must compensate the waiving buyer.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon view is that when two buyers have a stipulated option, each has an independent right to reject, unaffected by the other's waiver.

Khiyar al-Wasf: Missing Stipulated Description in a Slave
Ruling on khiyar al-wasf for a slave with stipulated skill

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for khiyar al-wasf when a stipulated description is missing and apply the principle that descriptions have no allocated portion of the price to distinguish valid from invalid conditions.

Core Idea
Descriptions in a sale have no price portion; if a stipulated description is missing, the buyer may keep or return the item.

This lesson examines a common scenario in sales: a buyer purchases an item based on a specific description (e.g., a skilled slave), but the item lacks that description. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling grounded in the principle that descriptions do not constitute part of the price. Understanding this ruling helps differentiate between valid options and invalid conditions that render a sale void.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the condition
A man buys a slave with the condition that the slave is a baker or a writer. The buyer later finds the slave does not possess that skill.
The condition is a desired description (wasf marghub fihi), not a defect.
2
State the ruling
The buyer has the option (khiyar) to either keep the slave at the agreed price or return him. If return is impossible (e.g., the slave is destroyed), the buyer gets a reduction in price.
This is the ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi position.
3
Understand the proof: the principle of descriptions
The ruling is based on the principle that descriptions do not have a portion of the price. The price is for the substance ('ayn). The condition is for the buyer's benefit; its failure means the buyer did not consent to the item without it, so he may rescind.
The proof is stated: 'because descriptions are not matched by any portion of the price'.
4
Distinguish from invalid conditions
If the condition is not a description but an unknown fact (e.g., a ewe is pregnant or yields a specific quantity of milk), the sale becomes invalid (fasid) due to gharar. However, stipulating 'milch' (halub) or 'lactating' (labun) is valid as it is a description.
The key is whether the condition is a known, observable description or an uncertain fact.
5
Address practical nuances
If the seller disputes the buyer's claim that the skill is missing, the buyer's word is taken. The slave must have the skill to the extent that the name (baker/writer) applies; if not, the buyer retains the option.
These details are from al-Ayni's Sharh al-Kanz and Majma' al-Anhur.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعبد مشترى بشرط خبزه أو كتبه ، ووُحِدَ بخلافه ، أُخِدٌ بِثَمَنِهِ أو تَرَكَهُ : لأنَّ الأوصاف لا يقابلها شيءٌ من الثَّمَن. والجواب : إن ثبوت الخيار لكلِّ واحدٍ منهما منفرداً ممنوع ، ألا ترى أنه إن وكل وليين ، فيثبت الوكالة لهما لا لأحدهما منفرداً وليس لأحدهما أن يتصرف بدون الآخر. [١]قوله : وعبد مشترى ؛ أي إن اشترى رجل عبداً بشرط كونه خبازاً أو كاتباً، فوجده المشتري بخلاف ما شرطه من الأوصاف، فالمشتري بالخيار إن شاء أخذه بثمنه المسمّى ، وإن شاء تركه إن كان ممكناً ، وإن تعدّر الردُّ لسبب من الأسباب رجع المشتري على البائع بالنقصان في ظاهر الرواية، وهو الأصح كذا في مجمع الأنهر (۳). (٢) قوله : لأن الأوصاف...الخ ؛ حاصله : أن كون العبد خبازاً أو كاتباً وصف مرغوب فيه، والأوصاف لا يقابلها شيء من الثمن، فيستحق في العقد بالشرط ، ويثبت لفواته الخيار ؛ لأنه لم يرضى بالعبدِ دونه. بخلاف ما لو باع شاءً على أنها حامل أو تحلب كذا وكذا رطلاً حيث يفسد البيع ؛ لأنه ليس من قبيل الوصف، وإنّما هو من قبيل الشّرط الفاسد إذ لا يعرف حقيقة ؛ لأنه يحتمل أنه لبن أو حمل او انتفاخ، حتى لو شرط أنه حلوب أو لبون لا يفسد ؛ لأنه وصف، ولو قال : يخبر كذا وكذا صاعاً ، ويكتب كذا قدراً يفسد البيع. ويشترط أن يقدر على الكتابة والخبز قدر ما يطلق عليه اسم الكاتب والخباز، وإن كان لا يحسنُ هذا المقدار فله الخيار، ولو قال البائع عند الردّ، كان يحسن ذلك ، لكنه نسي ذلك عندك، فالقولُ قولُ المشتري. كذا ذكره العيني في «شرح الكنز».
And a slave purchased with the condition of his baking or his writing, and is found contrary to that, he is taken with his price or left: because descriptions are not matched by any portion of the price. And the answer: The establishment of the option for each one individually is not allowed; do you not see that if he appoints two trustees, the agency is established for both, not for one individually, and it is not for one to act without the other. [1] His saying: 'And a slave purchased' means if a man buys a slave with the condition of him being a baker or a writer, and the buyer finds him contrary to what he stipulated of descriptions, then the buyer has the option: if he wishes he takes him for his named price, and if he wishes he leaves him if that is possible. And if rejection is prevented for some reason, the buyer recovers from the seller the decrease in price, according to the apparent narration, and it is the most correct. Thus in Majma' al-Anhur. (2) His saying: 'because descriptions...' etc.; its summary: That the slave being a baker or writer is a desired description, and descriptions are not matched by any portion of the price, so it is established in the contract by the condition, and for its loss the option is established because he did not consent to the slave without it. Unlike if he sold a ewe on the basis that it is pregnant or gives so many pounds of milk, where the sale is invalid because it is not of the category of description, but rather of the category of a corrupt condition since its reality is not known; because it could be milk, or pregnancy, or bloating. Even if he stipulated that it is milch or lactating, the sale is not invalid because it is a description. And if he said: it yields so many sa' of milk, or writes such amount, the sale is invalid. And it is a condition that he be able to write and bake to the extent that the name of writer or baker applies to him. And if he does not possess that amount, he has the option. And if the seller says at the time of rejection: 'He used to be skilled at that, but he forgot it with me', the word is the word of the buyer. Thus al-Ayni mentioned in Sharh al-Kanz.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
Ruling with proof. This passage discusses khiyar al-wasf (option due to missing description). When a slave is purchased with a stipulated condition that he is a baker or writer, and he is found to lack that skill, the buyer has the option either to keep the slave at the agreed price or to return him. The reason given is that descriptions (like being a baker) have no allocated portion in the price; rather, the price is for the essence of the item. The condition is for the buyer's benefit, and if the condition is unfulfilled, the buyer's consent is absent, so option is established. The commentary distinguishes this from cases where the condition is not a mere description but a fact that is unknown, such as a ewe being pregnant or yielding a specific amount of milk; such conditions render the sale invalid (fasid) because they are not known (gharar). However, stipulating that the ewe is 'milch' (halub) or 'lactating' (labun) is permissible as it is a description. The commentary also notes that if the description is a skill, the slave must have that skill to a reasonable degree; if not, the buyer has option. If return is impossible (e.g., the item is perishable), the buyer can claim a reduction in price. In a dispute, the buyer's word is taken. This is from the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) and is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'yah): Not directly discussed here but mentioned in previous lesson; option due to not seeing the item.
وصف مرغوب فيه (wasf marghub fihi): A desired description that adds value to the item but has no specific part of the price allocated to it.
الأوصاف لا يقابلها شيء من الثمن (al-awsaf la yuqabiluha shay' min al-thaman): A principle that descriptions in a sale do not have a specific portion of the price; the price is for the substance ('ayn).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A buyer purchases a slave with the condition that he is a baker, but finds he cannot bake. According to the Hanafi school, what are the buyer's options?
A) He may only accept a reduction in price.
B) He may keep the slave at the agreed price or return him.
C) He must return the slave; keeping is not allowed.
D) The sale is void because the condition was invalid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, khiyar al-wasf is established when a stipulated description (wasf marghub fihi) is missing, giving the buyer the option to rescind or claim a price reduction, based on the principle that descriptions have no portion of the price.

Ruling on Slave Purchased with Condition of Skill (Khiyar al-Shart)
Ruling on khiyar al-shart when a condition is not met

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the buyer's options when a stipulated attribute is missing and distinguish valid attribute conditions from invalid uncertain conditions.

Core Idea
A condition of a known attribute in a sale gives the buyer an option to cancel or accept with compensation; uncertain conditions void the contract.

When you buy an item based on a specific quality, what happens if that quality is absent? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling for a slave purchased with a condition of being a baker or writer. The buyer is given an option, but not all conditions are valid—uncertain conditions like 'pregnant' or 'yields X milk' corrupt the sale. Understanding the difference between a lawful attribute and an uncertain condition is crucial in sale contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is purchasing a slave with a condition (skill). The ruling: the buyer has khiyar al-shart (option) if the condition is not met.
The option is established for the buyer; he may take the slave at the price or cancel the sale.
2
Understand the basis for the option
Attributes are not priced separately in the price; the condition creates a right to the attribute, so its loss gives an option.
The reasoning is aqli (rational): since no part of the price is allocated to the attribute, the buyer did not consent to the slave without it.
3
Distinguish valid attribute conditions from invalid uncertain conditions
Known attributes (baker, writer) are valid conditions. Uncertain conditions like 'pregnant' or 'yields X milk' are invalid due to gharar and make the sale fasid.
The key is whether the condition is a definite, ascertainable attribute or a speculative outcome.
4
Note the consequence if return is impossible
If return is not possible (e.g., the slave has been used), the buyer recovers the diminution (naqsan) from the seller according to zahir al-riwayah.
This compensation is for the lost value due to the missing attribute.
5
Recognize the scope of the required skill
The slave must actually possess the skill to the extent that the name (baker/writer) applies. If not, the buyer has the option.
If the seller claims the slave had the skill but forgot, the buyer's word is taken.

And a slave purchased with a condition of his being a baker or a writer, and he was found contrary to that, he is taken with his price or left. Because attributes are not compensated by any part of the price. The answer: That the option is established for each one individually is prevented; do you not see that if he appointed two guardians, the agency is established for both, not for one individually, and neither has the right to act without the other. [Footnote:] His statement: 'And a slave purchased' means if a man buys a slave with the condition that he is a baker or writer, and the buyer finds him contrary to what was stipulated of attributes, then the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he takes him at the named price, and if he wishes, he leaves him if possible. And if return is prevented for some reason, the buyer recovers from the seller the diminution in the apparent narration, and that is the most correct, as in Majma' al-Anhur. His statement: 'Because attributes...' its gist: that the slave being a baker or writer is a desirable attribute, and attributes are not compensated by any part of the price, so he is entitled in the contract by virtue of the condition, and for its loss the option is established because he did not consent to the slave without it. Unlike if one sold a ewe on condition that it is pregnant or yields so many pounds of milk, then the sale is invalid because it is not from the category of attributes but rather from the category of a corrupt condition since its reality is not known; because it could be milk, pregnancy, or bloating. So if he stipulates that it is a milker or a milk-yielding one, it is not invalid because it is an attribute. And if he says: 'it yields so many sa' or 'writes so much', the sale is invalid. And it is required that he is able to write and bake to the extent that the name 'writer' and 'baker' applies to him; if he does not have that amount, he has the option. And if the seller at the time of return says, 'He was good at that, but he forgot it in your presence,' then the statement is of the buyer. Thus mentioned by al-Ayni in Sharh al-Kanz.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqaya deals with khiyar al-shart (option of condition) in sale contracts. The specific case is purchasing a slave with a stipulated attribute (being a baker or a writer). The ruling: if the slave is found lacking that attribute, the buyer has the option to either take the slave at the agreed price or cancel the sale. The reasoning is that attributes are not allocated a portion of the price; the price is for the essence. The condition creates a right to the attribute, and its loss gives the option. The commentary distinguishes this from selling a ewe with an uncertain condition like 'pregnant' or 'yields X milk', which renders the sale invalid due to uncertainty (gharar). Here, the condition is a known attribute. The text also discusses the extent of the required skill: the slave must actually be able to write and bake to a degree that qualifies him as a writer/baker. If not, the buyer has the option. In case return is impossible, the buyer gets compensation for the defect (naqsan) according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya). The author also notes that if the seller claims the slave had the skill but forgot, the buyer's word is taken (since the seller is a claimant).

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated by either party in the contract, usually for a specific condition to be met.
وصف (wasf): An attribute or quality of the subject matter that can be described and is known.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The buyer can only claim a reduction in price.
D) The sale is void automatically without any option.

Key Takeaway
When a stipulated attribute is missing, the buyer has the option to cancel the sale or keep it with compensation; uncertain conditions render the sale invalid.

The Option of Sight: Valid Sale Unseen with Right to Return
Introduction to khiyar al-ru'ya with hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling an unseen item, explain why khiyar al-ru'ya precedes khiyar al-ayb, and evaluate the hadith proof used to establish this ruling.

Core Idea
Selling unseen is valid but the buyer gets an option to return upon seeing — this option is stronger than the option of defect.

In this lesson, we enter the chapter on khiyar al-ru'ya (option of sight). The Hanafi school holds that a sale of an item not seen by the buyer is valid, but the buyer has a right to rescind upon seeing it. This ruling is based on a hadith that has been both connected and disconnected in transmission. The commentator explains why this option is presented before the option of defect, and defends the hadith against accusations of weakness. We will walk through the legal reasoning and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the ruling
The passage states: 'صح شراء...' meaning the sale of an unseen item is valid, and the buyer has the option upon seeing. Identify the act (sale of unseen item) and the consequence (buyer's right to rescind).
This is opposite to the view that such a sale is invalid.
2
Analyze the precedence
The commentator notes that khiyar al-ru'ya is presented before khiyar al-ayb because it is stronger. Why? Because khiyar al-ru'ya prevents the sale from fully concluding (it stops the sale from being complete), while khiyar al-ayb only prevents the sale from becoming binding after it is already complete.
Think of it as: one stops the train before it leaves the station, the other stops it after it has left.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith 'Whoever buys something he has not seen has the option when he sees it' is the primary evidence. Identify the wording: 'من اشترى شيئا لم يره فله الخيار إذا رآه'.
This is a general statement giving the buyer a choice upon sight.
4
Assess the authenticity defense
The commentator addresses criticism by al-Daraqutni that one narrator (Amr al-Kurdi) was weak. He defends by (1) citing a different chain from al-Nu'man ibn Bashir, (2) noting that Imam Muhammad narrated a mursal version, and (3) asserting that mursal hadith is accepted as proof in the Hanafi school.
This shows how Hanafi usul al-hadith principles (acceptance of mursal) support the ruling.
5
Synthesize the legal effect
The ruling: the sale is valid (sahih) but non-binding until the buyer sees the object. If the buyer chooses to return, it is returned without need for a defect. This option is established immediately upon sight.
This protects the buyer from purchasing something completely unknown.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في خيار الرؤية (صح شراء [١]قوله : فصل في خيار الرؤية ؛ قدّمه على خيار العيب ؛ لأنّ تأثير خيار الرؤية في منع تمام البيع، فكان أقوى من خيار العيب ؛ لكونه مؤثراً في منع لزوم الحكم. (٢) قوله : صح شراء...الخ ؛ لقوله : «من اشترى شيئا لم يره فله الخيار إذا رآه، روي مسنداً ومرسلاً : فالمسند ما أخرجَهُ الدَّارَ قُطْنِيُّ في «سننه» (۲) مسنداً عن داهر بن نوح عن عمرو بن إبراهيم بن خالد الكردي ، وعن وهب اليشكري عن محمد بن سيرين عن أبي هريرة ه، وقال عمر الكردي ، وأخبرني فضيل بن عياض عن هشام عن ابن سيرين عن أبي هريرة له مثله ، وقال عمر أيضاً، وأخبرني القاسم بن الحكم عن أبي حنيفة عن الهيثم عن محمد بن سيرين عن أبي هريرة له عن النبي له مثله. كذا في نصب الراية)) فان قلت : قال الدَّارَقُطْنِيُّ : عمر بن إبراهيم هذا يقال له الكردي يضع الأحاديث. (4) قلنا : رواه النعمان بن بشير عن النبي الا الله ، واحتج به الطحاوي)، ورواه محمد في كتاب المزارعة عن مجاهد، وطريق الطعن فيه من حيث الإرسال، والمرسل حجةٌ عندنا كما صرح به العلامة العَيْنِي وأما المرسل فرواه ابن أبي شيبة في مصنفه» (١) ، والدَّارَ قُطْنِي (٧) ثمّ البَيْهَقِي)
Chapter on the Option of Sight. (The sale is valid) [Footnote: His statement: Chapter on the Option of Sight; he presented it before the option of defect because the effect of the option of sight is to prevent the completion of the sale, so it is stronger than the option of defect, because it is effective in preventing the binding of the ruling. His statement: The sale is valid...etc.; because of his saying: 'Whoever buys something he has not seen has the option when he sees it,' narrated as both connected and disconnected: the connected is that which al-Daraqutni transmitted in his Sunan as connected from Dahir ibn Nuh from Amr ibn Ibrahim ibn Khalid al-Kurdi, and from Wahb al-Yashkuri from Muhammad ibn Sirin from Abu Huraira, and Amr al-Kurdi said, and informed me Fudayl ibn Iyad from Hisham from Ibn Sirin from Abu Huraira the like of it, and Amr also said, and informed me al-Qasim ibn al-Hakam from Abu Hanifa from al-Haytham from Muhammad ibn Sirin from Abu Huraira from the Prophet the like of it. Thus in Nasb al-Raya. If you say: al-Daraqutni said: This Amr ibn Ibrahim called al-Kurdi fabricates hadiths. We say: It was narrated by al-Nu'man ibn Bashir from the Prophet, and al-Tahawi argued by it, and Muhammad narrated it in Kitab al-Muzara'ah from Mujahid, and the way of criticism is from the aspect of interruption, and the interrupted hadith is a proof according to us as stated by Allamah al-Ayni. As for the interrupted, it was narrated by Ibn Abi Shayba in his Musannaf, and al-Daraqutni, then al-Bayhaqi.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on khiyar al-ru'ya (option of sight). The commentator explains why this chapter precedes the chapter on khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect): because the option of sight prevents the sale from becoming complete and binding, whereas the option of defect prevents the sale from becoming binding after it is complete. Thus the former has a stronger effect. The main ruling: a sale of an unseen item is valid, but the buyer has the option upon seeing it. This is based on the hadith: 'Whoever buys something he has not seen has the option when he sees it.' The commentator then addresses the authenticity of this hadith. Two versions are mentioned: a musnad (connected chain) and a mursal (disconnected). The musnad is attributed to al-Daraqutni, but its chain includes Amr al-Kurdi, whom al-Daraqutni accused of fabricating hadiths. The commentator defends the hadith by noting that it was also narrated from al-Nu'man ibn Bashir with a different chain, and al-Tahawi used it as proof. Additionally, Imam Muhammad narrated a mursal version in Kitab al-Muzara'ah, and according to the Hanafi school, mursal hadiths are valid as proof. Thus the ruling is established.

Key Terms
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'ya): The option to rescind a sale after seeing the object if it was purchased unseen.
مرسل (mursal): A hadith where the companion is omitted from the chain; the successor narrates directly from the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the commentator present the chapter on khiyar al-ru'ya before the chapter on khiyar al-'ayb?
A) Because the option of sight is stronger as it prevents the completion of the sale.
B) Because the option of defect is weaker and comes later.
C) Because the option of sight is mentioned in the Quran.
D) Because the author preferred alphabetical order.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates the sale of unseen items and grants the buyer a powerful option upon sight, supported by a hadith that is defended through multiple chains and the acceptance of mursal narrations.

Option of Inspection (Khiyar al-Ru'yah): Hanafi Position and Proofs
Establishes validity of buying unseen goods with option of inspection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on khiyar al-ru'yah, identify the proofs adduced, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Buying unseen is valid because the buyer can reject upon inspection — ignorance does not cause dispute.

This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-ru'yah, establishing that a sale of an unseen specified item is valid. The author marshals a hadith, the practice of Companions, and a rational argument, then contrasts with the Shafi'i position which invalidates the contract due to jahalah. This lesson will guide you through the proofs and the inter-madhhab disagreement.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school rules the sale of an unseen specified item as valid (sahih) with the buyer having the option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah).
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i holds the sale invalid (batil) due to jahalah (ignorance) of the subject matter.
3
Follow the Hanafi proofs
Examine the three proofs: the hadith, the incident of Uthman and Talha, and the rational argument that ignorance does not lead to dispute.
The hadith is shadh but accepted via multiple chains and the Hanafi acceptance of mursal.
4
Analyse the Shafi'i counter-argument
Understand that the Shafi'i objection is based on gharar and the principle that any uncertainty invalidates the contract.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Hanafi law, the buyer may keep or return the item; under Shafi'i law, the contract is void ab initio.

فصل في خيار الرؤية صح شراء ما لم يره لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم من اشترى شيئا لم يره فله الخيار إذا رآه روي مسنداً ومرسلاً فالمسند ما أخرجه الدارقطني في سننه مسنداً عن داهر بن نوح عن عمرو بن إبراهيم بن خالد الكردي وعن وهب اليشكري عن محمد بن سيرين عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه وقال عمر الكردي وأخبرني فضيل بن عياض عن هشام عن ابن سيرين عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه مثله وقال عمر أيضاً وأخبرني القاسم بن الحكم عن أبي حنيفة عن الهيثم عن محمد بن سيرين عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مثله كذا في نصب الراية فان قلت قال الدارقطني عمر بن إبراهيم هذا يقال له الكردي يضع الأحاديث قلنا رواه النعمان بن بشير عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم واحتج به الطحاوي ورواه محمد في كتاب المزارعة عن مجاهد وطريق الطعن فيه من حيث الإرسال والمرسل حجة عندنا كما صرح به العلامة العيني وأما المرسل فرواه ابن أبي شيبة في مصنفه والدارقطني ثم البيهقي وهو في سننهما حدثنا اسماعيل بن عياش عن أبي بكر بن عبد الله بن أبي مريم عن مكحول رفعه إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وقال من اشترى إلى آخره وزاد إن شاء أخذه وإن شاء تركه قال الدارقطني هذا مرسل وأبو بكر بن أبي مريم ضعيف كذا ذكره العلامة الزيلعي ولما روي أن عثمان رضي الله عنه باع أرضاً له بالبصرة من طلحة بن عبيد الله رضي الله عنه فقيل لطلحة رضي الله عنه إنك قد غبنت فقال لي الخيار لأني اشتريت ما لم أره وقيل لعثمان رضي الله عنه إنك قد غبنت فقال لي الخيار لأني بعت ما لم أره فحكما جبير بن مطعم رضي الله عنه فقضى بالخيار للطلحة وكان ذلك بمحضر من الصحابة كذا في المنح ولأن الجهالة لعدم الرؤية لا تفضي إلى المنازعة لأنه لو لم يوافقه بعد الرؤية يرده على البائع فصار لجهالة الوصف في المعاين المشار إليه وصورته اشترى ثوباً مشاراً إليه غير معلوم عدد ذرعاته فإنه يجوز لكونه معلوم العين وإن كان ثمة جهالة لأنها لا تفضي إلى المنازعة قوله شراء ما لم يره صورته أن يقول البائع للمشتري بعتك الثوب الذي في كمي هذا وصفته كذا وكذا أو الدرة التي في حقيبتي هذه وصفتها كذا وكذا وعلى هذا القياس قوله خلافاً للشافعي فإنه لا يصح العقد عنده أصلاً لأن المبيع
Chapter on the Option of Inspection. Purchasing what one has not seen is valid, based on his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever buys something he has not seen has the option when he sees it.' It is narrated as both connected and disconnected. As for the connected (musnad), al-Daraqutni narrated it in his Sunan from Dahir ibn Nuh from Amr ibn Ibrahim ibn Khalid al-Kurdi, and from Wahb al-Yashkuri from Muhammad ibn Sirin from Abu Hurayra (may Allah be pleased with him). And Amr al-Kurdi said: Fudayl ibn Iyad told me from Hisham from Ibn Sirin from Abu Hurayra (may Allah be pleased with him) similar to it. And Amr also said: al-Qasim ibn al-Hakam told me from Abu Hanifa from al-Haytham from Muhammad ibn Sirin from Abu Hurayra (may Allah be pleased with him) from the Prophet (peace be upon him) similar to it. Thus in Nasb al-Raya. If you say: al-Daraqutni said: This Amr ibn Ibrahim, called al-Kurdi, fabricates hadiths. We say: al-Nu'man ibn Bashir narrated it from the Prophet (peace be upon him), and al-Tahawi relied on it, and Muhammad narrated it in Kitab al-Muzara'a from Mujahid. The criticism of it is from the angle of it being mursal, and the mursal is a proof according to us, as stated by al-Allama al-Ayni. As for the mursal version, Ibn Abi Shayba narrated it in his Musannaf, and al-Daraqutni, then al-Bayhaqi. It is in their Sunan: Ismail ibn Ayyash narrated to us from Abu Bakr ibn Abdullah ibn Abi Maryam from Makhul, raising it to the Prophet (peace be upon him), and he said: 'Whoever buys...' to the end, and added: 'If he wishes, he takes it, and if he wishes, he leaves it.' Al-Daraqutni said: This is mursal, and Abu Bakr ibn Abi Maryam is weak. Thus mentioned by al-Allama al-Zaylai. And because it is narrated that Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) sold land belonging to him in Basra to Talha ibn Ubaydullah (may Allah be pleased with him). It was said to Talha (may Allah be pleased with him): 'You have been cheated.' He said: 'I have the option because I bought what I did not see.' And it was said to Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him): 'You have been cheated.' He said: 'I have the option because I sold what I did not see.' So they appointed Jubayr ibn Mut'im (may Allah be pleased with him) as arbitrator, and he decided the option in favor of Talha, and this was in the presence of the Companions. Thus in al-Minh. And because ignorance due to lack of sight does not lead to dispute, because if he does not agree after seeing it, he returns it to the seller; so it becomes like ignorance of description in a designated object. Its example: he bought a designated garment, the number of its yards unknown; it is valid because the object is known, even if there is ignorance, because it does not lead to dispute. His statement: 'purchasing what one has not seen' – its form: the seller says to the buyer: 'I sell you the garment that is in my sleeve, its description such and such,' or 'the pearl that is in my bag, its description such and such,' and analogously. His statement: 'contrary to al-Shafi'i' – for the contract is not valid at all according to him, because the sold item...
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof on the option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah) in sales. It opens by stating the Hanafi position: it is valid to purchase an item one has not personally seen, and the buyer has the right to either accept or reject the item upon actual inspection. The author then provides the primary textual evidence: the hadith 'Whoever buys something he has not seen has the option when he sees it.' He discusses the chain of transmission, noting that some narrators have been criticized. However, the Hanafi school accepts this hadith because it has multiple supporting chains, including a musnad narration and a mursal narration, and according to Hanafi usul, a mursal hadith is a valid proof. Additionally, he cites the practice of the Companions: the incident of Uthman and Talha, where both parties claimed the option for unseen goods, and Jubayr ibn Mut'im ruled in favor of the buyer, in the presence of other Companions without objection, indicating a tacit consensus. The author then gives a rational argument: the ignorance caused by lack of sight does not lead to dispute because the buyer can simply return the item if unsatisfied, analogous to purchasing a specific item whose description is unknown. The passage ends by stating the Shafi'i position: the contract is entirely invalid because the object of sale is unknown, constituting gharar. This sets up the inter-madhhab dispute: Hanafis validate the contract with an option, while Shafi'is invalidate it outright.

Key Terms
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'yah): The buyer's right to rescind or affirm a contract upon seeing the purchased item for the first time after the contract.
مرسل (mursal): A hadith narrated by a successor directly from the Prophet without mentioning a Companion.
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty about a crucial aspect of the contract, such as the exact description of the object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person buys a garment he has never seen, what is the legal status of the contract?
A) The contract is invalid because the object is unknown.
B) The contract is valid, and the buyer has the option to return upon inspection.
C) The contract is valid only if the seller provides a full description.
D) The contract is suspended until the buyer sees the item.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates the sale of an unseen specified item, granting the buyer the option of inspection, based on hadith, Companion practice, and the principle that inspectable ignorance does not lead to dispute.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Khiyar al-Ru'ya: The Hanafi Position on Unseen Goods Sales
Explains the Hanafi position on khiyar al-ru'ya with evidence and refutes Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sale of a specific unseen object and explain how the Hanafi school distinguishes between validity (sihha) and bindingness (luzum), while contrasting with the Shafi'i position that deems the sale invalid.

Core Idea
A sale of a specific unseen object is valid in the Hanafi school but the buyer retains an option to cancel upon inspection.

The sale of an item that the buyer has not yet seen presents a classic point of ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. In this passage, the author lays out the Hanafi position that such a contract is valid (sahih) but non-binding (ghayr lazim), supported by hadith and Companion practice. The Shafi'i school, by contrast, rules the contract void due to uncertainty (jahalah). This lesson unpacks the evidence and the legal distinction that underlies the difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the sale of an unseen specific object is valid but the buyer has an option to void upon seeing (khiyar al-ru'ya). Note that the contract is non-binding (ghayr lazim) due to this option.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the contract is invalid (fasid or batil) because the object is unknown (majhul), and selling an unknown item is prohibited.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof is based on the general rule that jahalah (ignorance) invalidates a sale. They consider the description essential; without seeing, the description is unknown, so the contract is void.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response differentiates between the identity of the object (al-dhat) and its description. The object is known by pointing (mu'ayyan), so ignorance of description does not affect the core of the contract but only its bindingness. The buyer can return the item if dissatisfied, preventing dispute.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Shafi'i, the contract is void, so ownership never transfers and the buyer must return the item and get a full refund. Under Hanafi, ownership transfers immediately but the buyer has a unilateral right to rescind upon inspection, making the contract effectively a provisional sale.

كتاب البيع خيار الرؤية ما لم يره خلافا للشافعي وهو في سننهما: حدثنا اسماعيل بن عياش عن أبي بكر بن عبد الله بن أبي مريم عن مكحول رفعه إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، وقال: «من اشترى... إلى آخره، وزاد: إن شاء أخذه وإن شاء تركه». قال الدارقطني: هذا مرسل وأبو بكر بن أبي مريم ضعيف. كذا ذكره العلامة الزيلعي. ولما روي «أن عثمان باع أرضا له بالبصرة من طلحة بن عبيد الله رضي الله عنهما، فقيل لطلحة: إنك قد غبنت، فقال: لي الخيار؛ لأني اشتريت ما لم أره، وقيل لعثمان: إنك قد غبنت، فقال: لي الخيار؛ لأني بعتُ ما لم أره، فحكما جبير بن مطعم رضي الله عنه، فقضى بالخيار لطلحة، وكان ذلك بمحضر من الصحابة». كذا في «المنح». ولأن الجهالة لعدم الرؤية لا تفضي إلى المنازعة؛ لأنه لو لم يوافقه بعد الرؤية يرده على البائع، فصار لجهالة الوصف في المعاين المشار إليه، وصورته: اشترى ثوبا مشارا إليه، غير معلوم عدد ذرعاته، فإنه يجوز لكونه معلوم العين، وإن كان ثمة جهالة؛ لأنها لا تفضي إلى المنازعة. [١] قوله: شراء ما لم يره؛ صورته: أن يقول البائع للمشتري: بعتك الثوب الذي في كمي هذا وصفته كذا وكذا، أو الدرة التي في حقيبتي هذه وصفتها كذا وكذا، وعلى هذا القياس. [٢] قوله: خلافا للشافعي، فإنه لا يصح العقد عنده أصلا؛ لأن المبيع مجهول، وبيع المجهول فاسد، وفي كمال الدراية نقلا عن «الإيضاح»: «لا خلاف في أن غير المرئي مجهول الوصف، لكن جهالة الوصف عند الشافعي تؤثر في صلب العقد؛ لأن الوصف مقصود، وعندنا: لا يؤثر فيه، بل في صفته، وهي اللزوم؛ لأن المعقود عليه الذات، باعتبار المالية وهي موجودة في غير المرئي». انتهى. [١] قوله: ولمشتريه الخيار؛ فيه إشارة إلى أن الخيار لا يمنع ثبوت الملك في البدلين، بل يمنع لزومه، قال القهستاني ناقلا عن «المحيط»: «لو باع دينا بدين فلا خيار لهما، ولو باع عينا بعين كان لهما الخيار». [٢] قوله: عندها؛ فيه أنه يوهم أنه لا يجوز له الفسخ قبل الرؤية، وليس كذلك، بل له فسخ العقد قبل الرؤية، كما صرح به في «فتاوى قاضي خان». وقال في «البحر» نقلا عن «المحيط»: «قيل: لا يملك فسخه قبلها، وقيل: يملكه، وهو الأصح؛ لأن الفسخ كما يملك بالخيار يملك بسبب عدم لزوم البيع كالعارية والوديعة والوكالة والشركة، وعدم اللزوم ثابت؛ لسبب جهالة المبيع». انتهى والجواب أن هذا الفسخ للخلل في الرضاء لا للخيار، فلا إشكال. [٣] قوله: إلى أن... الخ؛ في «البحر»: «اختلفوا هل هو مطلق أو مؤقت، فقيل: مؤقت بوقت إمكان الفسخ بعدها، حتى لو تمكن منه، ولم يفسخ سقط خياره، وإن لم توجد الإجازة صريحا ولا دلالة، وقيل: يثبت الخيار له مطلقا، فيكون له الفسخ في بيع عمره ما لم يسقط بالقول أو بفعل يدل على الرضا، وهو الصحيح؛ لإطلاق النص، والعبرة لعين النص لا لمعناه». [٤] قوله: وإن رضي قبلها؛ أي بالقول؛ فإنه لو أجازه بالفعل بأن تصرف فيه كالإعتاق والتدبير وغيرهما زال خياره.
Book of Sales: Option of Inspection – What he has not seen, contrary to al-Shafi'i. And it is in their Sunan: Isma'il ibn 'Ayyash narrated from Abu Bakr ibn 'Abdullah ibn Abi Maryam from Makhul raising it to the Prophet ﷺ, and he said: 'Whoever buys...' to the end, and added: 'If he wishes he takes it, and if he wishes he leaves it.' Al-Daraqutni said: This is mursal and Abu Bakr ibn Abi Maryam is weak. Thus mentioned by al-Zayla'i. And based on what was narrated: 'That 'Uthman sold a land of his in Basra to Talha ibn 'Ubaydullah, and it was said to Talha: You have been cheated. He said: I have the option because I bought what I have not seen. And it was said to 'Uthman: You have been cheated. He said: I have the option because I sold what I have not seen. So they appointed Jubayr ibn Mut'im as arbitrator, and he decided the option for Talha, and that was in the presence of the Companions.' Thus in al-Manh. And because ignorance due to lack of sight does not lead to dispute; because if he does not agree after seeing it, he returns it to the seller. So it becomes like ignorance of description in a physically pointed-out object. Its example: He bought a pointed-out garment, the number of yards unknown; it is valid because it is known in identity, even though there is ignorance, because it does not lead to dispute. [1] His statement: 'Purchase of what he has not seen'; its form is that the seller says to the buyer: I sell you the garment that is in my sleeve, its description such and such, or the pearl that is in my bag, its description such and such, and analogously to this. [2] His statement: 'Contrary to al-Shafi'i'; for according to him the contract is not valid at all because the sold item is unknown, and selling the unknown is invalid. In Kamal al-Diraya, quoting from al-Idah: 'There is no dispute that an unseen item is unknown in description, but this ignorance of description according to al-Shafi'i affects the core of the contract because description is intended; according to us, it does not affect the core but affects its binding nature because the object of contract is the substance, in terms of monetary value, and that exists in the unseen.' End. [1] His statement: 'And the buyer has the option'; therein is a reference that the option does not prevent the establishment of ownership in the countervalues, but prevents its bindingness. Al-Qahistani said, quoting from al-Muhit: 'If one sold a debt for a debt, there is no option for them; if one sold a physical object for a physical object, they have the option.' [2] His statement: 'Upon seeing it'; therein is an implication that he may not revoke before seeing, but it is not so; rather, he has the right to revoke the contract before seeing, as clarified in Fatawa Qadi Khan. And it is said in al-Bahr, quoting from al-Muhit: 'It is said: He does not possess the power to revoke before seeing; and it is said: He does possess it, and this is the correct view, because revoking, as it is possessed through option, is also possessed due to the absence of bindingness of the sale, like 'ariyah (loan), wadi'ah (deposit), wakalah (agency), and shirkah (partnership), and the absence of bindingness is established because of the ignorance of the sold item.' End. And the answer is that this revocation is due to a defect in consent, not due to the option, so there is no difficulty. [3] His statement: 'Until...' etc. In al-Bahr: 'They differed whether it is absolute or time-bound. It was said: It is time-bound to the time when revocation after seeing is possible, so that if he is able to revoke and does not revoke, his option lapses, even if explicit or implicit acceptance did not occur. And it was said: The option remains absolute, so he may revoke throughout his life as long as he does not drop it by statement or by an act indicating satisfaction, and this is the correct view, due to the unrestricted text, and consideration is given to the text itself, not its meaning.' [4] His statement: 'Even if he is satisfied before seeing'; i.e., by statement; for if he accepts it by action, such as by disposing of it through emancipation, tadbir, or other actions, his option lapses.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the sale of unseen goods (khiyar al-ru'ya). The Hanafi position is that such a sale is valid but the buyer has the option to void the contract upon seeing the item. The Shafi'i position, stated as 'contrary to al-Shafi'i', is that the contract is void ab initio because the object is unknown. The author provides evidence: a hadith (though weak and mursal) and the well-known incident of 'Uthman and Talha where the Companions decided in favour of the option, implying consensus. The Hanafi rational argument is that ignorance of description in a physically identified object does not lead to dispute because the buyer can simply return it. The commentary then elaborates that the option does not affect the transfer of ownership (al-milk) but only the bindingness (luzum); thus the contract is valid but non-binding. The option becomes active upon seeing, but the buyer may revoke even before seeing due to the contract's non-binding nature. The duration of the option is debated: some say it is limited to a time after seeing, but the correct (sahih) view is that it is absolute until the buyer drops it by word or action. If the buyer expresses satisfaction before seeing, that does not cancel the option unless he performs an act indicating acceptance (e.g., freeing a slave or otherwise disposing of the item). The text also notes that if the item is sold debt for debt, there is no option, but if both are specific physical items, the option exists.

Key Terms
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'ya): The right of the buyer of an unseen good to cancel the contract after inspecting the item.
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty about the sold item's description or quantity.
لزوم (luzum): Bindingness; the quality of a contract that makes it non-revocable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in the passage, what is the legal status of a sale where the buyer purchases a specific unseen object?
A) The sale is void (batil) because the object is unknown.
B) The sale is valid but non-binding, and the buyer has the option to cancel upon seeing.
C) The sale is valid and binding immediately, with no option.
D) The sale is suspended until the buyer sees and approves.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between validity (sihha) and bindingness (luzum); a sale of a specific unseen object is valid but gives the buyer an absolute option to cancel upon inspection.

Khiyar al-Ru'yah: Duration and Effect of Prior Consent
Expanding the ruling on khiyar al-ru'yah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-ru'yah, distinguish between absolute and time-limited views, and identify what invalidates the option.

Core Idea
Prior verbal consent does not waive the option of inspection; only action or explicit words after seeing do.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the buyer's right to rescind after seeing an item bought unseen. It clarifies that this option is not lost by mere verbal consent before seeing, and it explores whether the option is absolute or time-limited. Understanding this requires distinguishing between consent in words and consent by action, and recognizing that true consent depends on knowledge of the item.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is khiyar al-ru'yah? It is an option for the buyer who purchases an item without seeing it. Determine its legal status: it is a permissible right, not a duty.
The option prevents the contract from becoming binding until the buyer sees the item and accepts or rejects.
2
Determine the duration of the option
Two views exist: one says it is time-limited (lapses after a reasonable opportunity to rescind), the other says it is absolute (lasts until waived). Identify which is the preferred view and its evidence.
The preferred view is absolute, based on the generality of the text (iṭlāq al-naṣṣ).
3
Analyse the effect of prior verbal consent
Why does saying 'I am pleased' before seeing not waive the option? Because true consent requires knowledge of the item's qualities, which is impossible before seeing.
The contract is non-binding before seeing due to lack of knowledge.
4
Identify invalidators of the option
List actions or words that waive the option: explicit verbal acceptance after seeing, or actions implying acceptance (e.g., selling, manumitting). Prior verbal consent is not an invalidator.
Consent by action is effective because it demonstrates actual satisfaction.
5
Examine the intra-madhhab dispute on rescission procedure
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require the seller's presence when the buyer rescinds; Abu Yusuf allows rescission without the seller. Note which view is relied upon for fatwa.
The mufta bihi view is that rescission is valid without the seller's presence.

Source Text

ولِمْشَتَرِيهِ الخِيارُ عندها إلى أن يُوجَدَ مُبْطِلُه وإِن رَضِيَ قبلها. [1] قوله: ولمشتريه الخيار؛ فيه إشارة إلى أن الخيار لا يمنع ثبوت الملكِ في البدلين، بل يمنع لزومه. [2] قوله: عندها؛ فيه أنه يوهم أنه لا يجوز له الفسخ قبل الرؤية، وليس كذلك، بل له فسخ العقد قبل الرؤية، كما صرح به في «فتاوی قاضي خان». [3] قوله: إلى أن... الخ؛ في «البحر»: «اختلفوا هل هو مطلق أو مؤقت، فقيل: مؤقت بوقت إمكان الفسخ بعدها، حتى لو تمكن منه، ولم يفسخ سقط خياره، وإن لم توجد الإجازة صريحاً ولا دلالة، وقيل: يثبت الخيار له مطلقاً، فيكون له الفسخ في بيع عمره ما لم يسقط بالقول أو بفعل يدلُّ على الرّضا، وهو الصحيح؛ لإطلاق النص، والعبرة لعين النّصّ لا لمعناه». [4] قوله: وإن رضي قبلها؛ أي بالقول؛ فإنه لو أجازه بالفعل بأن تصرف فيه كالإعتاق والتدبير وغيرهما زال خياره. [1] قوله: يكون له حق الفسخ؛ لأن هذا الخيار تعلق ثبوته بالرؤيا فكان عدماً قبلها، فلا يصح إسقاطه قبلها. فإن قيل: لو كان عدماً قبل الرؤية لما كان له حق الفسخ قبلها. أجيب: بأن حق الفسخ قبلها ليس برضاء؛ لأن الرّضاءَ به لا يتحقق إلا برؤيتِهِ بحكم الخيار، بل لأنه عقد غيرُ لازم، حتى لو ردّه قبل الرؤية ليس له أن يرضى عندها. واعلم أن الفسخ بخيار الرؤية لا يحتاج إلى قضاء ولا رضاء، لكنَّه لا يصح إلا بحضرة البائع عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد، وقال أبو يوسف: يصح بغير حضرته أيضاً، والرضاء يصح بدون حضرته. [2] قوله: إذا رآه؛ المراد بالرؤية: العلم بالمقصود، فهو من عموم المجاز؛ لوجود مسائل اتفاقية لا يكتفى بالرؤية فيها؛ مثلاً إذا كان المبيع مما يعرف بالشم كمسك اشتراه وهو يراه، فإنه إنما يثبت الخيار له عند شمه، فله الفسخ عند شمه لعدم رؤيته، وكذا لو رأى شيئا ثم اشتراه فوجده متغيّراً؛ لأن هذه الرؤية غير معرفة للمقصود الآن، وكذا شراء الأعمى يثبت له الخيار عند الوصف له، فأقيم فيه الوصف مقام الرؤية. [3] قوله: بحكم أنه... الخ؛ لأن صحة الفسخ تعتمد لزوم العقد، والعقد هاهنا قبل الرؤية غير لازم، لكن الخلل في الرّضاء؛ إذ هو عبارة عن الاستحسان، واستحسان الشيء مع الجهل بأوصافه لا يتحقق، واللزوم يعتمد تمام الرضاء، وتمامه بالعلم بأوصاف هي مقصودة، وإنما تصير معلومة بالرؤية؛ فلذا لا يعتبر قوله: رضيت قبل الرؤية.
And the buyer has the option at the time of seeing until an invalidator of it is found, even if he expressed consent before it. [1] His statement: 'And the buyer has the option' indicates that the option does not prevent the establishment of ownership in the two exchanges, but rather prevents its bindingness. [2] His statement: 'at the time of seeing' suggests that he is not allowed to rescind before seeing, but this is not the case; rather, he may rescind the contract before seeing, as stated in Fatawa Qadi Khan. [3] His statement: 'until...' etc.; in al-Bahr: 'They differed: is it absolute or time-limited? It was said: time-limited to the time when rescission becomes possible after seeing, so that if he is able and does not rescind, his option lapses, even if no express or implicit acceptance occurred. And it was said: the option is established absolutely, so he may rescind for the rest of his life as long as he does not waive it by words or an action indicating consent—this is the correct view, due to the generality of the text, and consideration is given to the literal wording, not its meaning.' [4] His statement: 'even if he expressed consent before it' means verbally; for if he consented by action, such as by disposing of it like manumission, tadbir, etc., his option is removed. [1] His statement: 'he has the right to rescind' because this option's establishment depends on seeing, so it is non-existent before it, thus waiving it before seeing is invalid. If it is objected: If it were non-existent before seeing, he would not have the right to rescind before it. The answer: The right to rescind before seeing is not by virtue of consent, because consent cannot be realized without seeing by virtue of the option, but rather because the contract is non-binding. Thus if he returns it before seeing, he cannot consent at the time of seeing. Know that rescission by the option of inspection does not require a court order or the other's consent, but according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad it is only valid in the presence of the seller, while Abu Yusuf said it is valid without his presence as well, and consent is valid without his presence. [2] His statement: 'when he sees it' means knowledge of the intended (quality); this is a general metaphor, because there are agreed cases where mere sight is insufficient. For instance, if the sold item is known by smell, like musk which he bought while seeing it, the option is only established when he smells it, so he may rescind upon smelling because he has not seen it. Similarly, if he saw something then bought it and found it changed, this sight does not indicate the intended (quality) now. Similarly, a blind person's purchase: the option is established when it is described to him, so description stands in place of sight. [3] His statement: 'by virtue of it being...' etc., because the validity of rescission depends on the bindingness of the contract. Here, before seeing, the contract is non-binding, but the defect is in consent, for it is approval, and approval of something while ignorant of its qualities cannot be realized. Bindingness depends on complete consent, and completion of consent is by knowledge of the intended qualities. These are only known through seeing, so his saying 'I consented before seeing' is not considered.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on khiyar al-ru'yah (option of inspection) for the buyer. The base text states that the buyer has the option upon seeing until an invalidator is found, even if he verbally expressed consent before seeing. The commentator clarifies that the option does not prevent ownership but prevents the contract from becoming binding. He notes that the option can be exercised before seeing as well, because the contract is non-binding due to ignorance of the item. There is a dispute among Hanafis about whether the option is absolute or time-limited; the preferred view is that it is absolute, lasting until explicitly or implicitly waived. Consent by action (e.g., manumission) waives the option, but mere verbal consent before seeing does not. The commentator also explains that 'seeing' means knowledge of the intended quality; thus, for items known by smell (like musk), smelling suffices, and for a blind person, description suffices. Regarding rescission, it does not require court or the seller's consent, but according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, it must be done in the seller's presence; Abu Yusuf allows it otherwise. The reasoning is that the defect is in the consent, which is incomplete without knowledge of the item's qualities.

Key Terms
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'yah): The option for the buyer to rescind a contract after seeing an item bought unseen, due to lack of knowledge of its qualities.
مبطل (mubtil): That which invalidates the option, such as explicit waiver or actions implying acceptance.
الرضا (al-rida): Consent; in this context, complete consent requires knowledge of the item's qualities, hence prior verbal consent is ineffective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in the Hanafi school, what is the duration of khiyar al-ru'yah for the buyer?
A) It is limited to three days after seeing.
B) It is absolute and lasts until waived explicitly or implicitly.
C) It lasts only until the buyer touches the item.
D) It expires automatically after one year.

Key Takeaway
The buyer's option of inspection is absolute and only waived by explicit or implicit acceptance after gaining knowledge of the item.

Seller Does Not Have Option of Inspection
Ruling statement on seller's option of inspection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the seller's option of inspection and explain the intra-Hanafi development of the position.

Core Idea
The seller has no option of inspection; only the buyer does, and this is the established Hanafi position despite initial analogy.

This passage clarifies a subtle point: although one might think both parties should have the option of inspection when the item is unseen, the Hanafi school settled that only the buyer enjoys this right. The text reveals an intra-Hanafi development where Abu Hanifa originally held the opposite view before retracting. Let's explore the reasoning behind the final position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage explicitly states: the seller does not have an option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah) when he sells something he has not seen.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Note the initial intra-Hanafi difference
The commentator mentions that Abu Hanifa initially held the seller also has the option, drawing an analogy with the option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb) and option of condition (khiyar al-shart).
This shows that the ruling was not immediately settled.
3
Understand why the initial view was abandoned
The analogy was deemed imperfect because the seller is presumed to know what he sells, whereas the buyer needs protection from ignorance. Thus, the option is exclusive to the buyer.
The retraction by Abu Hanifa strengthens the final position.
4
Confirm the operative ruling
The school consensus, reflected in zahir al-riwayah, is that the seller has no such option. This is the relied-upon view.
Any fatwa today must follow this position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(لا لبائعه): أي إذا باع شيئا لم يَرَهُ لا يكون له الخيار إذ رآه. [4] قوله: لا يكون له...الخ؛ وكان أبو حنيفة يقول أولاً: إن الخيار للبائع أيضاً اعتباراً بخيار العيب والشرط، فإن خيار العيب لا يختص بالمشتري، بل إذا وجد البائع
(Not for its seller): i.e., if he sells something he has not seen, he does not have the option when he sees it. [4] His statement: 'he does not have...' etc.; Abu Hanifa initially used to say that the option is for the seller as well, by analogy with the option of defect and condition, for the option of defect is not exclusive to the buyer—rather, if the seller finds...
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that the seller does not have the option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah) when selling something unseen. The commentator notes that Abu Hanifa initially held the opposite view, drawing an analogy with khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect) which applies to both parties. However, he later abandoned this view, and the established position of the school is that only the buyer has this option. The reasoning is that the buyer's option protects against ignorance of the purchased item, whereas the seller is presumed to know what he sells.

Key Terms
خيار العيب (khiyar al-'ayb): Option of defect: the right to rescind upon discovery of a hidden defect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who has the option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah) according to the final Hanafi position?
A) Both buyer and seller.
B) Only the buyer.
C) Only the seller.
D) Neither party.

Key Takeaway
The seller has no right to cancel upon seeing the item he sold unseen; this is the relied-upon Hanafi position.
